Abidjan, located in Ivory Coast, is classified as one of the Districts of Côte d'Ivoire. It covers a total area of 2,119.0 square kilometers and sits at an elevation of 18.0 meters above sea level. The city operates within the GMT time zone, with a UTC offset of +0, and uses the area code +225. Abidjan is home to a population of 6,321,017 people, who are referred to as Abidjanais. The city's motto is "District d'Abidjan, acteur de développement." Serving as the largest city in both Ivory Coast and the Lagunes Region, Abidjan is also the capital of the Lagunes Region, the Sud Department of Ivory Coast, and is recognized as the capital in the context of crime in Ivory Coast. The Parliament of Ivory Coast is located in Abidjan, as are notable sites such as the Culture Palace of Abidjan and Village Ivoire. The city is also the location of the headquarters for organizations including the Democratic Party of Ivory Coast – African Democratic Rally, Incubateur Régional d'Afrique de l'Ouest, and Interivoire. Abidjan is a significant center for education and culture, hosting the campus of CIFAD and the University of Science and Technology of Ivory Coast. Universal Music Africa has its city location in Abidjan, and the city is the hometown of Magic System and rapper Ak47. The Ivorian Republican Guard has its garrison in Abidjan, and the city is home to sports grounds for JC d'Abidjan, Stade d'Abidjan, and Stella Club d'Adjamé. Major sporting events such as the 1984 African Cup of Nations Final and the 2009 African Nations Championship Final have taken place in Abidjan. Several notable individuals are connected to the city. Priscille Kreto, Robert Sankara, and Roger Aholou were born in Abidjan, while Robert Guéï, Christian Bonaud, and Christian Lattier died there. Marcel Blaguet Ledjou is associated with Abidjan through his occupation. Additionally, Abidjan is the location of the headquarters for Interivoire and Incubateur Régional d'Afrique de l'Ouest. Village Ivoire, the Culture Palace of Abidjan, and Universal Music Africa are all situated in the city. The Democratic Party of Ivory Coast – African Democratic Rally and Interivoire have their headquarters in Abidjan as well. The city is also referenced as a country in the context of Sub-Saharan Africa.
Addis Ababa, the capital city of Ethiopia, is also recognized as one of the regions of the country. It covers a total area of 527.0 square kilometers, with a land area of 527,000,000.0 square meters, and sits at an elevation of 2,354.8848 meters above sea level. The city has a population of 2,739,551, resulting in a population density of 5,165.1 people per square kilometer. Residents of Addis Ababa are known as Addis Ababans. The city operates in the East Africa Time zone, with a UTC offset of +3, and its area code is (+251) 11. Founded by Menelik II and Taytu Betul, Addis Ababa has played a significant role in the history and governance of Ethiopia. It has served as the capital for various governments, including the Derg, the People's Democratic Republic of Ethiopia, and the Transitional Government of Ethiopia. The city has also been the site of notable historical events such as the Battle of Segale, the 1960 Ethiopian coup d'état attempt, and the 1989 Ethiopian coup d'état attempt. Several important institutions and organizations are based in Addis Ababa. The headquarters of the Prosperity Party, the Development Bank of Ethiopia, and the United Ethiopian Democratic Forces are all located in the city. The Commercial Bank of Ethiopia Headquarters is also situated here. Educational institutions such as Unity University, which has both its campus and city location in Addis Ababa, and the Royal College, Addis Abeba, are part of the city's academic landscape. Menelik II School is another notable educational establishment in the city. Addis Ababa is home to a number of significant buildings and centers, including the Dembel City Center and Betoch. The city also hosts the assembly plants for vehicles such as the Tofaş Şahin and the Hyundai Ioniq. The Metals and Engineering Corporation and Enat Bank have their city locations in Addis Ababa as well. The city is a hub for sports and military organizations. Defence Force S.C., Ethio Electric S.C., and Saint George S.C. all have their grounds in Addis Ababa. Military units such as Mehal Sefari, the 65th Infantry Division "Granatieri di Savoia," and Kebur Zabagna have been garrisoned in the city. Addis Ababa has been the birthplace of several notable individuals, including Rophnan, Sayat Demissie, and Meron Getnet. It is also the hometown of Endegna, Walias Band, and Getatchew Mekurya. The city has been the place of death for figures such as Caleb Meakins, Belay Zeleke, and Dawit Nega. Additionally, Hizkias Assefa received his education in Addis Ababa. Prominent residents of the city include Oumer Hussein, Ahmed Shide, and Abune Mathias. The city is also the location of the campus of Unity University and the Royal College, Addis Abeba. Finally, Sub-Saharan Africa is listed as a country associated with Addis Ababa, though the city is officially part of Ethiopia.
Adelaide, located in Australia, has a total population of 1,387,290. The city is home to notable places such as Castle Plaza and Prescott Schools, and it also serves as the setting for "Sam Fox: Extreme Adventures." Several individuals have significant connections to Adelaide. Cricketer Cameron Williams, as well as Carl Tietjens and Carlee Taylor, were born there. Additionally, Adelaide is the place where Carl Linger, Pāvils Dreijmanis, and Quentin Kenihan passed away.
Ahmedabad, a metropolis in India, is governed by the Amdavad Municipal Corporation under a mayor–council government system. The city covers a total area of 505.0 square kilometers, with an urban area of 1,866,000,000.0 square meters, and sits at an elevation of 53.0 meters above sea level. It has a total population of 8,253,000, and its residents are known as Ahmedabadi or Amdavadi. Ahmedabad operates in the Indian Standard Time zone, with a UTC offset of +5:30. The area code for the city is 079, and its postal code is 380 0XX. Historically, Ahmedabad served as the capital of both the Gujarat Sultanate and Gujarat under the Mughal Empire. The city is the location of several notable sites, including the Calico Dome, Sanskar Kendra, and Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel International Airport. The airport itself is situated in Ahmedabad, as are institutions such as the Entrepreneurship Development Institute of India and Smt. NHL Municipal Medical College. Ahmedabad is also recognized as the assembly location for vehicles such as the Suzuki Baleno (subcompact), the third generation of the Suzuki Dzire, and the sixth generation of the Suzuki Swift. The city is home to the headquarters of organizations like the Bochasanwasi Akshar Purushottam Swaminarayan Sanstha, DD Girnar, and Colors Gujarati. The Gujarat Titans play their home games in Ahmedabad, and the 11th Indian Infantry Division is garrisoned in the city. Several individuals have strong connections to Ahmedabad. Amit Dave, Pradipsinh Jadeja, and Priti Sengupta were born there, while Prahalad Chunnilal Vaidya, Pranlal Kharsani, and Pransukh Nayak passed away in the city. Nikhil Paramjit Sharma, Disha Vakani, and Sheba Chhachhi received their education in Ahmedabad. The city is also the hometown of Meghdhanush (band), Mauli Dave, and the duo Shyamal-Saumil. Pradip Parmar, Rengaswamy Ramesh, and Mavji Desai reside in Ahmedabad. Various organizations and businesses are based in or serve the region, including Adani Ports & SEZ, the Care Institute of Medical Sciences, and Calico Mills (Ahmedabad Manufacturing and Calico Printing Mills). The Gujarat Metro Rail Corporation Limited lists Ahmedabad as its predecessor. SVP Hospital and Ahmedabad Civil Hospital are located in the region, while MylesCar, Jasuben Pizza, and the Ahmedabad Municipal Transport Service serve the city. Ahmedabad is also the nearest city to Vastrapur Lake, the Indian Wild Ass Sanctuary, and Kankaria Lake.
Algiers, the capital city of Algeria, is situated near the Mediterranean Sea and operates within the Central European Time zone, with a UTC offset of +01:00. The city covers a total area of 363.0 square kilometers, while its metropolitan area extends to 1,190,000,000.0 square kilometers. Algiers has a total population of 4,510,000, with a population density of 12,424.0 people per square kilometer in the city proper and 7,012.0 in the metropolitan area. The area code for Algiers is (+213) 021, and its postal codes range from 16000 to 16132. As the capital, Algiers has served as the seat of government for several entities, including French Algeria, the Provisional Government of the French Republic, and the Provisional Government of the Algerian Republic. The city is also the headquarters for organizations such as the Democratic National Rally, Samira TV, and the Canary Islands Independence Movement. Additionally, the Supreme Council of the Arabic Language in Algeria is based in Algiers. Algiers is home to a number of significant institutions and landmarks. The Roma Italian School of Algiers, the Electricity and Gas Regulation Commission, and the Botanical Garden Hamma are all located in the city. The University of Science and Technology Houari Boumediene and the National Polytechnic School (Algeria) are both situated within Algiers. The city is also notable for its association with the stylistic origins of Sanaa music and for being the region where Tajine Mtewem is popular. Several important historical events have taken place in Algiers, including the Capture of Peñón of Algiers in 1529, the Battle of Algiers from 1956 to 1957, and the Battle of Bab El Oued. The city has also hosted major sporting events, such as the 2010, 2011, and 2012 Algerian Cup Finals. Football teams like USM El Harrach, NA Hussein Dey, and USM Alger have played their seasons in Algiers. The city serves as a garrison for the Commodore-in-Charge, the Republican Guard of Algeria, and the Algerian Land Forces. The Renault Dauphine was assembled in Algiers, and the city is home to the headquarters of the Algeria Press Service and the Public Establishment of Television. Algiers has been the birthplace of notable individuals such as Roger Hanin, Samira Negrouche, and Baya El Hachemi. It is also the hometown of Amel Brahim-Djelloul, Biyouna, and Julie Pietri. The city has been the place of death for figures like Saïd Bouhadja, Léon Carré, and Léon Cauvy. Adam Larfi and Inès Ibbou reside in Algiers, while Jean-Baptiste Nouvion is associated with the city as a spouse. John McAslan is linked to Algiers through significant buildings, and Henry Stanyford Blanckley is noted for his occupation in the city. Through its rich history, diverse institutions, and vibrant cultural life, Algiers stands as a central hub in Algeria, reflecting its importance as both a political and cultural capital.
Almaty is the largest city in Kazakhstan and is classified among the list of cities in the country. It covers a total area of 682.0 square kilometers, with a metropolitan area spanning 9,395,000,000.0 square meters. The city has a population of 1,977,011 and uses the area code +7 727. Postal codes in Almaty range from 050000 to 050063. The city operates in the UTC+6 time zone, with a corresponding UTC offset of +6. Almaty is governed by the Almaty City Mäslihat. Historically, Almaty served as the capital of the Kazakh Soviet Socialist Republic. Today, it remains a significant urban center, hosting a variety of important institutions and landmarks. The President's Residence, Satbayev Memorial Museum, and Sayran Lake are all located within the city. Jeltoqsan is also a notable place in Almaty. Several prominent individuals are associated with Almaty. Roman Chentsov, Roman Kirsch, and Sanzhar Mustafin were born in the city, while Boris Blinov, Boris Katalymov, and Uzakbay Karamanov passed away there. Yesken Sergebayev is known for notable work related to Almaty. The city is also the hometown of Holy Dragons, Liza Umarova, and Deniz Reno, and serves as the residence for Zarina Diyas, Timur Khabibulin, and Aleksandr Nedovyesov. Almaty is a hub for various organizations and events. Bek Air targets the city’s airport, and Hyundai H350 vehicles are assembled there. Qazaq Radiosy and Satbayev University are based in Almaty, as are the headquarters of Prime Aviation, the Rukhaniyat Party, and the Democratic Party Adilet. The city was the site of the 2013 Asian Shotgun Championships and the 2021 Almaty City Mäslihat election. The Central Asian Military District, the Central Military Band of the Ministry of Defense of Kazakhstan, and the Internal Troops of Kazakhstan all have garrisons in Almaty. Sports teams such as AFC Kairat, FC Alma-Ata, and FC Megasport use the city as their ground. Almaty Arena is operated by the city. Almaty is also closely connected to several natural and recreational sites. Big Almaty Lake, Shymbulak, and Charyn National Park are all located near the city. Additionally, Medeu District and Akbulak, Kazakhstan, are classified as types of Almaty.

Residents of the city are known as Ammani. The city uses the area code +962(6), and its postal codes range from 11110 to 17198. Amman operates on a UTC offset of +3. The city has also been the site of significant historical events, such as the Battle of Nablus in 1918, the First Battle of Amman, and the First Battle of the Jordan. Several notable individuals have connections to Amman: Rouzbahan Fraij, Sama'a Khraisat, and Sami al-Oraydi were born there, while Behnam Abu Alsoof, Samir Al-Rifai, and Samir Ghawshah passed away in the city. Amman serves as a key hub for transportation and healthcare. Queen Alia International Airport is located in the city, and DHL International Aviation ME targets Amman as an airport destination. The Jordan Hospital and the Specialty Hospital, Jordan, are both situated in Amman, as are the Prince Hamza Hospital, Arab Medical Center, and King Hussein Cancer Center. The city is also home to the National Orthodox School and Princess Sumaya University for Technology. Several organizations and companies have their headquarters or main offices in Amman, including the American Center of Research, Ammon News, and Roya TV. Zara Investment Holding, Jobedu, and Tamatem Games are based in the city as well. The Royal Jordanian Air Force, the Royal Jordanian Army, and the 3rd Armored Division (Jordan) all have their garrisons in Amman. Amman has played a central role in the history of the region, serving as the capital not only of modern Jordan but also during the Jordanian annexation of the West Bank and the Emirate of Transjordan. The Lada Niva is assembled in the city. Historical figures such as Zubayr ibn al-Awwam and Henri Vanwaetermeulen have been involved in battles associated with Amman. The city is also the hometown of musical groups like JadaL, El Morabba3, and Akher Zapheer. Notable residents include Bayan Tal, Julyana Al-Sadeq, and Lina Attel. Nasser Judeh received his education in Amman.
Amsterdam, located in the Netherlands, serves as both a municipality and the capital of the country. The city covers a total area of 219.32 square kilometers, with 165,760,000 square meters of land and 53,560,000 square meters of water. Amsterdam lies at an elevation of -2.0 meters. Its postal codes range from 1000 to 1183, and the area code is 020. The population totals 907,976, and residents are known as Amsterdammers. The city operates under the governance of the Municipal Council of the Netherlands. Amsterdam observes Central European Time and Central European Summer Time, with UTC offsets of +1 and +2, respectively. The city’s motto is "Heldhaftig, Vastberaden, Barmhartig," which translates to "Valiant, Steadfast, Compassionate." Several notable locations and events are associated with Amsterdam. The Amsterdam Museum and the Press Museum are both situated in the city, as is Prins Hendrikkade. Amsterdam has also been the site of significant historical events, including the Bijltjesoproer, the Anabaptist riot, and Operation Ramrod 16. A number of individuals have strong ties to Amsterdam. Calvin Jong-a-Pin, Calvin Mac-Intosch, and Calvin Valies were all born in the city. Additionally, Cab Kaye, Caesar ten Cate, and Carel Victor Gerritsen died in Amsterdam.
Ankara, the capital city of Turkey, is also classified as one of the metropolitan municipalities in the country. It covers a total area of 24,521.0 square kilometers, with an urban area spanning 2,767,850,000.0 square meters. The city sits at an elevation of 938.0 meters above sea level and has a population of 5,747,325, resulting in a metropolitan population density of 234.0 people per square kilometer. Residents of Ankara are known as Ankarans. The city uses the area code 1 and the postal code format 06xxx. It operates in the Time in Turkey time zone, with a UTC offset of +3. Ankara was founded by Mustafa Kemal Atatürk and serves as the capital for both Turkey and the Government of the Grand National Assembly, as well as for the historical Ankara Eyalet. The city is home to several important institutions and landmarks, including the headquarters of the Capital Markets Board of Turkey, the Ministry of Culture and Tourism, and the Progressive Republican Party. The General Staff of the Turkish Armed Forces, the Gendarmerie Search and Rescue Battalion Command, and the Gendarmerie Special Operations all have their garrisons in Ankara. Several notable buildings in Ankara are associated with architects such as Vedat Tek and Cengiz Bektaş. The city is also the location of the Presidential Complex of Turkey. Ankara hosts the campuses of Ankara Yıldırım Beyazıt University and Başkent University, and the Ankara University Faculty of Veterinary Medicine is situated within the state. The city is the site of significant events, including the 2012 Turkish Cup Final, the 1962 Turkish coup d'état attempt, the Battle of Ancyra, and the Siege of Ankara. Ankara is a center for industry and manufacturing, with companies such as GAMA Enerji, Turkish Aerospace Industries, and ASFAT based in the city. It is also the assembly location for vehicles like the MAN Lion's City and the Neoplan Skyliner. The city is the nearest urban center to Dikmen Vadisi. Several sports teams, including Bağlumspor, Sitespor, and Çubukspor, have their grounds in Ankara. The city is also the hometown of musical groups such as RockA and Nükleer Başlıklı Kız, as well as the cellist Benyamin Sönmez. Ankara has been the birthplace of notable individuals such as Cahit Zarifoğlu, Can Dündar, and Cansu Dere. It is also the place where Pınar Köksal, Samim Bilgen, and Sarkis Minassian passed away. Osman Kavala received his education in Ankara, while Beytullah Kayışdağ, Sadık Savaş, and Salih Aydın reside in the city. Philip S. Kosnett is associated with Ankara through his occupation. The Roman Baths of Ankara are among the city's historical sites. The city also serves as the location for the headquarters of the Capital Markets Board of Turkey and the Ministry of Culture and Tourism.

The Presidential Administration of Kazakhstan is both headquartered in and located within the city. The Presidential Park and Saryarka Velodrome are among the notable locations within Astana. The city also hosts the headquarters of key governmental ministries and is the site of significant events and institutions, further solidifying its status as the heart of Kazakhstan.

Baghdad, the capital city and a major metropolis of Iraq, covers a total area of 673.0 square kilometers and is situated at an elevation of 34.0 meters above sea level. The city was founded by Al-Mansur on July 30, 762, and its residents are known as Baghdadis. Baghdad operates under a mayor–council form of government and observes a UTC offset of +3. The city’s postal codes range from 10001 to 10090. Baghdad has played a central role in the history and governance of the region, serving as the capital for entities such as the Coalition Provisional Authority, the Arab Federation, and Mandatory Iraq. The city is also the state location for the College of Science at the University of Baghdad and is home to the University of Al-Ma'mun. Several organizations, including the Progress Party (Iraq), the Ministry of Planning (Iraq), and Journal Iraq, have their headquarters in Baghdad. The city is also the base for Voice of Iraq and has hosted events such as the 1986 Iraqi Perseverance Cup. Baghdad is a significant hub for transportation and military operations. Jupiter Airlines and DHL International Aviation ME both target Baghdad as an airport destination, while the Al-Abid launch site is located within the city. The United States Forces – Iraq, the Sixth Army of the Ottoman Empire, and the 6th Division of Iraq have all maintained garrisons in Baghdad. The city is also the site of Al-Rasheed SC’s ground. Several notable military and historical events have taken place in Baghdad, including the Camp Liberty killings and the captures of Baghdad in 1624 and 1638. Military installations such as Camp Cropper, Camp Liberty, and Camp Nama are also located in the city. Baghdad has been the birthplace of figures such as Carmel Eliash, Amira Nur al-Din, and Qais Al-Sindy. It is also the place where Amira Nur al-Din, Qasim Mahmoud, and Qays Abd al-Hussein al-Yasiri passed away. The city is the hometown of Motez, Namir (singer), and Simor Jalal. Jawad Saleem is known for his notable work in Baghdad, and Hisham N. Ashkouri has received an award associated with the city. Ibn al-Tilmidh held an occupation in Baghdad, while Al-Mustansir II was a predecessor in the city. Barham Salih, Denha I, and Sabrisho IV have all had their residences in Baghdad. The city is also the location for the headquarters of the Coalition Provisional Authority and the Arab Federation. The College of Science at the University of Baghdad is situated in Baghdad, and the city is the state for this institution. The city’s rich history, diverse population, and central role in Iraq’s governance and culture make it a significant metropolis in the region.

Brasília, the federal capital of Brazil, serves as the country's administrative center and is also the capital of the Fourth Brazilian Republic and the period in the History of Brazil from 1985 to the present. Founded on April 21, 1960, the city is situated at an elevation of 1,172 meters and covers a total area of approximately 5,801.998 square kilometers. Its metropolitan population numbers 4,291,577, with a population density of 480.827 inhabitants per square kilometer. Residents of Brasília are known as Brasiliense. The city operates within the Time in Brazil time zone, with a UTC offset of −03:00. Its area code is +55 61, and the postal code is 70000-000. The headquarters of the Progressistas party, the Brazilian Antarctic Program, and the Brazilian Democratic Movement are also located there. Fundação Getulio Vargas maintains a campus in Brasília, and the University of Brasília is situated in the city as well. The city has hosted notable events such as the 2009 and 2010 Aberto de Brasília tennis tournaments, as well as the 2020 and 2021 editions of the Supercopa do Brasil. Sports teams like Centro de Futebol Zico de Brasília Sociedade Esportiva and Real Brasília FC play their home games in the city. Furthermore, Antonio Palocci, Celso Amorim, and Erenice Guerra have resided in Brasília. The city’s significance is further highlighted by its role as the location for the headquarters of the Brazilian Antarctic Program and the Brazilian Democratic Movement, as well as being the region served by Eletrobras Furnas.

Residents of Conakry include Cellou Dalein Diallo, Fodéba Isto Keira, and Shekuba Saccoh. Geographically, Conakry is the nearest city to both Baie de Sangareya and the Atlantic Ocean, further emphasizing its importance as a coastal and urban center in Guinea.

Residents of Phnom Penh are referred to as Phnom Penher, and the city uses the area code +855(023). Phnom Penh operates under the time zone known as Time in Cambodia, with a UTC offset of +07:00. The municipal council serves as the city's form of government. Several notable institutions and organizations are located in Phnom Penh, including the Cambodian Center for Human Rights, Canadia Bank, and the Roman Catholic Cathedral of Phnom Penh. The city has played a significant role in Cambodian history, serving as the capital during the periods of Cambodia (1953–1970) and Democratic Kampuchea. It was the site of major historical events, including the Cambodian–Spanish War, the 1997 Cambodian coup d'état, and the Fall of Phnom Penh. The battle involving Dien Del also took place here. The city is the hometown of Doch Chkae and Yeun Savuth, and it is the residence of Bun Kenny and Bun Rany. Cambodian Sign Language is spoken in Phnom Penh. Boeung Kak is the nearest city to Phnom Penh. The city is also the location of the campus for the Department of Media and Communication at the Royal University of Phnom Penh.

Several notable organizations and landmarks are situated in Reykjavík. Carbon Recycling International, Hof Ásatrúarfélagsins, and Reykjavík Cathedral are all located within the city. Educational institutions such as Endurmenntun Háskóla Íslands and Reykjavik Women's Gymnasium are based in Reykjavík, as is Reykjavík Airport. The city also serves as the ground for sports clubs like Léttir, Valur (men's football), and ÍR men's football. Reykjavík is the headquarters for the Home Rule Party (Iceland), Responsible Future (Iceland), and the newspaper DV. Companies such as Arctica Finance, Vodafone Iceland, and Sagafilm have their city location in Reykjavík. The city is also the hometown of musical groups including Amiina, Merzedes Club, and Daughters of Reykjavík. The Vatnsmýrin Nature Reserve and the Atlantic Ocean are the nearest natural features to Reykjavík. The city is part of the region served by Borgarspítalinn and Landspítali hospitals, as well as by businesses like Mikkeller and Bæjarins Beztu Pylsur. Reykjavík is associated with several individuals. Páll Guðlaugsson, Páll Logason, and Pétur Georg Markan were born in the city, while Páll Gíslason, Benedikt G. Waage, and Birgir Örn Birgis passed away there. Eva Dögg Sæmundsdóttir resides in Reykjavík.
Riga, the capital city of Latvia, serves as one of the administrative divisions of the country and is governed by the Riga City Council. The city covers a total area of 2,046.0 square kilometers, with a land area of 2,046,000,000.0 square meters and a water area of the same size. Water makes up approximately 15.8 percent of Riga’s total area. The metropolitan area extends to 3,359,000,000.0 square meters and supports a population of 870,000 people. Riga uses the area codes 66 and 67, and observes a UTC offset of +2 and +3. Several notable locations and events are associated with Riga. Riga has also been the site of significant historical battles, including the Battle of Dahlenkirchen, the Battle of Jugla, and the Battle of Riga in 1215. Additionally, Robert Pflug, Roberts Lapainis, and Roberts Mūrnieks died in the city.
Rio de Janeiro, located in Brazil, is recognized as one of the country's major cities. It was founded on March 1, 1565, and is governed by the Municipal Chamber of Rio de Janeiro under a mayor–council government system. The city is situated at an elevation of 2.0 meters above sea level and is known by the demonym "Carioca." Covering a total area of 1,221.0 square kilometers, Rio de Janeiro has a total population of 6,747,815. The metropolitan area is significantly larger, spanning 4,539,800,000.0 square meters, with a metropolitan population of 12,280,702 and a population density of 2,705.1 people per square kilometer. The city operates within the Time in Brazil time zone, with a UTC offset of minus three hours. Its area code is 21, and postal codes in Rio de Janeiro range from 20000-001 to 23799-999. As a prominent urban center, it is included in the list of cities in Brazil. Several notable locations and events are associated with Rio de Janeiro. The park Campo de Santana, the shopping center CasaShopping, and the television series "Caminhos do Coração" are all situated in the city. The city is also linked to various notable individuals. Cacá Bueno, Caetano (footballer), and Caio Couto were born in Rio de Janeiro, while Cafuringa, Café Filho, and Caio César died in the city.

Riyadh is also notable for its educational institutions, such as Prince Sultan University and Princess Nora bint Abdul Rahman University, both of which are located in the city. The 2008 Saudi Crown Prince Cup Final took place in Riyadh. In the realm of sports, Al-Diriyah Club, Al-Shaeib FC, and Al Shabab FC (Riyadh) all have their grounds in the city. Adnan al-Aroor is also linked to Riyadh through his occupation. The Riyadh Military Hospital and King Abdulaziz Medical City are both located within the region of Riyadh. The city was the site of the Battle of Riyadh in 1902.

Rotterdam is a city and municipality located in the Netherlands. It is governed by the Municipal Council of the Netherlands and is classified both among the list of cities in the Netherlands by province and the list of municipalities of the Netherlands. Rotterdam observes Central European Time (CET) with a UTC offset of +1, and during the summer months, it follows Central European Summer Time (CEST) with a UTC offset of +2. Salvador, Bahia, located in Brazil, is classified among the municipalities of the country. The city was founded on March 29, 1549, and stands at an elevation of 8 meters above sea level. Salvador is featured as a location in the series “Vai Anitta.” It is also the nearest city to the Bay of All Saints, the Baía do Iguape Marine Extractive Reserve, and the Atlantic Ocean.

San José is the nearest city to Braulio Carrillo National Park and Juan Castro Blanco National Park. The 2002 San José mayoral election took place in Costa Rica, with San José as the country. The city’s influence extends to human rights in Costa Rica, as it is recognized as the capital in this context as well.

Adam Smith was born in Fife on June 5, 1723, and died in Edinburgh on July 17, 1790. He is recognized as a figure within Western philosophy and was influenced by thinkers such as Richard Cantillon, Francis Hutcheson, and Aristotle. Smith authored notable works including "The Wealth of Nations" and "The Theory of Moral Sentiments." His legacy extends into academic disciplines, as evidenced by Tom Campbell, a philosopher whose field of study includes Adam Smith. Additionally, Smith served as the predecessor to Walter Campbell of Shawfield in a particular tenure.
Adolf Hitler was born on April 20, 1889, in Braunau am Inn. Over the course of his life, he became associated with both the German Workers' Party and the Nazi Party. He was married to Eva Braun. Hitler died in Berlin on April 30, 1945, with the cause of his death being recorded as the Death of Adolf Hitler.
Alan Turing was born on June 23, 1912, in Maida Vale and died on June 7, 1954, in Wilmslow. The cause of his death was cyanide poisoning. He pursued his education at the University of Cambridge and Princeton University, where he earned a Master of Arts degree. Turing's doctoral advisor was Alonzo Church, and he later became the doctoral advisor to Robin Gandy and Beatrice Worsley. His academic work spanned the disciplines of cryptanalysis, logic, and computer science. Turing is renowned for his contributions to the cryptanalysis of the Enigma machine, the development of the Turing test, and Turing's proof. He was also the developer of Turochamp. His achievements were recognized with the award of Smith's Prize. Turing was influenced by Max Newman, and in turn, he influenced figures such as Jonathan Bowen and Cicely Popplewell. Alonzo Church, who advised Turing, counted him among his doctoral students, while Robin Gandy, one of Turing's own students, was guided by him during his doctoral studies.
Albert Einstein was born on March 14, 1879, in Ulm. He later died on April 18, 1955, in Princeton, New Jersey. Throughout his life, Einstein held citizenship in Cisleithania and the Free State of Prussia, and he also experienced a period of statelessness. His academic discipline was physics, and he was notably influenced by figures such as Hendrik Lorentz and Hermann Minkowski. Alfred Kleiner served as his doctoral advisor, and Einstein himself became Kleiner’s doctoral student. Einstein was recognized for his significant contributions to science, including the ensemble interpretation, Bose–Einstein statistics, and the EPR paradox. His achievements were honored with awards such as the Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, the Copley Medal, and membership in the National Academy of Sciences. He was also a key person at the Davos University Conferences and authored "The Meaning of Relativity." In addition to his scientific work, Einstein starred in the film "Atomic Power." In his personal life, Einstein was married to Mileva Marić and later to Elsa Löwenthal, who is also known as Elsa Einstein. He had children, including Lieserl Einstein and Hans Albert Einstein, and was a parent to members of the Einstein family, such as Eduard Einstein. Hans Albert Einstein was one of his children, and Samarendra Kumar Mitra was among those influenced by his work.
Aleister Crowley, whose birth name was Edward Alexander Crowley, was born in Warwickshire on October 12, 1875. He received his education at Malvern College, Tonbridge School, and Eastbourne College, and later attended Trinity College, Cambridge. Crowley became known for his diverse occupations as a novelist, mountaineer, and occultist. Among his notable works are "Moonchild," "The Blue Equinox," and "777 and Other Qabalistic Writings of Aleister Crowley," all of which he authored. His influence extended to figures such as Robert Anton Wilson, Lionel Snell, and Wilfred Talbot Smith. Crowley was married to Rose Edith Kelly. He died in East Sussex on December 1, 1947. His legacy continued to inspire subsequent works, including "The Magical Revival."
Alexander Fleming was born on August 6, 1881, in Darvel. He pursued his education at the University of Westminster, Imperial College London, and St Mary's Hospital Medical School. Fleming specialized in the fields of bacteriology and immunology. He became widely known for his discovery of penicillin and his work on lysozyme. Throughout his distinguished career, he received several honors, including being named a Fellow of the Royal Society, being awarded the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine, and being appointed a Knight Bachelor. Alexander Fleming passed away on March 11, 1955.
Alexander Graham Bell was born as Alexander Bell on March 3, 1847, in Edinburgh. He was the son of Alexander Melville Bell. Bell later became a Canadian citizen under Canadian nationality law. He is best known for the invention of the telephone and for his association with the AT&T Corporation. In addition to his work on the telephone, Bell founded several organizations, including Bell Canada, AT&T Corporation, and AT&T Laboratories. Bell was also an accomplished designer and builder. His birth year was 1847, and he passed away in 1922. For further information, he is associated with the IMDb identifier 0956089.
Alfred Joseph Hitchcock was born on August 13, 1899, in Leytonstone. He attended St Ignatius' College and Salesian College, Battersea, as part of his education. His professional career began in 1919 and continued until 1980. Hitchcock was married to Alma Reville, and together they had a child named Pat Hitchcock. He passed away on April 29, 1980. Throughout his life, Hitchcock was recognized for his significant contributions to film and television. He was the creator of "Alfred Hitchcock Presents" and directed notable films such as "Psycho" (1960), "Rope," and "Murder!" In addition to directing, he produced "Psycho," "Rope," and "Under Capricorn." His talents also extended to writing, as he was the writer for "Murder!," "Blackmail" (1929), and "Rich and Strange." Hitchcock was involved in editing the 1928 film "Champagne." He was also credited as the author of "Lifepod" (1993). Hitchcock's influence extended beyond his own works. He starred in productions such as "Truffaut" and "The World of Alfred Hitchcock." His achievements have been recognized with numerous awards and nominations. C. M. Woolf is known for his association with Hitchcock. The director's legacy is marked by his enduring impact on cinema and television, as well as his extensive body of work spanning over six decades.
Alfred the Great was active from 871 to 886 and was the son of Osburh and Æthelwulf, King of Wessex. He succeeded Æthelred I of Wessex, who was his predecessor, and was later succeeded by his own son, Edward the Elder. Alfred was married to Ealhswith, and together they had several children, including Edward the Elder, Æthelweard, and Ælfthryth, Countess of Flanders. During his reign, Alfred the Great commanded forces in significant battles such as the Battle of Ashdown, the Battle of Basing, and the Battle of Chippenham. After Alfred's reign, Edward the Elder became his successor, continuing the royal lineage.
Ali Mazrui was born on February 24, 1933, in Mombasa and was of Kenyan origin and nationality. He pursued his higher education at several prestigious institutions, including Manchester University, Oxford University, and Columbia University. Mazrui was known for his work on Black orientalism and had a distinguished career as an author and academic, as well as holding other professional roles. Amartya Sen was born on November 3, 1933, in the British Raj. He pursued his education at the University of Calcutta, earned a Master of Arts degree, and continued his studies at Trinity College, Cambridge. Sen is renowned for his contributions to development economics, welfare economics, and social choice theory. His work has been influenced by thinkers such as John Rawls, Mary Wollstonecraft, and Gautama Buddha. Throughout his distinguished career, Sen has received several prestigious awards, including the Bharat Ratna, the Johan Skytte Prize in Political Science, and the National Humanities Medal. He is the author of notable works such as "Development as Freedom," "Inequality Reexamined," and "The Idea of Justice." In addition to his scholarly achievements, he founded the Human Development and Capability Association. Sen's personal life includes his marriage to Nabaneeta Dev Sen, and he is the parent of Antara Dev Sen and Nandana Sen. He was succeeded by Martin Rees in a tenure position. Furthermore, Amartya Sen appeared in the film "Nobelity."
Amos Oz, born Amos Klausner on May 4, 1939, in Mandatory Palestine, was an Israeli novelist and journalist. Over the course of his distinguished career, he received several notable awards, including the Prince of Asturias Awards, the Bialik Prize, and the Goethe Prize. Oz was the author of acclaimed works such as "My Michael," "A Perfect Peace," and "A Tale of Love and Darkness." In addition to his literary achievements, he was also the writer of the film "My Michael." Amos Oz held Israeli nationality under Israeli nationality law. He passed away in Petah Tikva on December 28, 2018.
Andrei Sakharov was born in Moscow on May 21, 1921, and he also passed away in the same city on December 14, 1989. He was a Russian physicist whose academic pursuits encompassed nuclear physics and physical cosmology. Sakharov studied at Moscow State University and the Lebedev Physical Institute, where his doctoral advisor was Igor Tamm. Over the course of his career, he became known for his work on proton decay, electromagnetic pulse, and baryogenesis. Sakharov was recognized with several prestigious awards, including the Elliott Cresson Medal, the Nobel Peace Prize, and the Lenin Prize. He held citizenship in the Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic. Beyond his scientific achievements, Sakharov played a significant role in human rights advocacy, founding the Committee on Human Rights in the USSR and serving as a key figure in the Memorial society.
Archimedes was born and died in Sicily. He was a prominent figure in the fields of mathematics, mechanics, and engineering. His work was influenced by Eudoxus of Cnidus, and he himself became a significant influence on later thinkers such as René Descartes and Gerolamo Cardano. Archimedes is renowned for several important contributions, including Archimedes' principle, Archimedes' screw, and the concept of the lever. He authored works such as "On Floating Bodies" and "On the Equilibrium of Planes."
Aristotle was born in 384 BCE in Stagira, an ancient city, and died in 322 BCE in the ancient kingdom of Macedonia. He is associated with the tradition of Western philosophy and was influenced by figures such as Empedocles, Parmenides, and Hippias. Aristotle’s legacy has been significant, with individuals like Manuel Chrysoloras, John Corcoran, and Octavius Freire Owen being particularly known for their work related to him.
Arthur Currie began his service in 1897 and was a member of the Canadian Expeditionary Force. He played a significant role in World War I, serving as a commander in several major battles, including the Battle of Amiens in 1918, the Battle of Cambrai in 1918, and the Battle of Hill 70. Throughout his career, Currie received numerous honors, such as the Croix de guerre from both Belgium and France, as well as the Order of the Crown from Belgium. In addition to his military achievements, he was associated with McGill University and Khaki University. Arthur Currie was succeeded by Arthur Eustace Morgan in a tenure, with Morgan's predecessor being Currie himself.
Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington, was born as Arthur Wesley on May 1, 1769, in Dublin. He was the son of Garret Wesley, 1st Earl of Mornington, and later became the father of Arthur Wellesley, 2nd Duke of Wellington. On September 14, 1852, he died in Walmer. He was married to Catherine Wellesley, Duchess of Wellington, and their marriage was reciprocated, as she was also his spouse. Wellesley was associated with both the Conservative Party (UK) and the Tories political faction. Throughout his distinguished career, he played a significant role as a military commander, leading forces in the Campaign in south-west France in 1814, as well as at the Battle of Argaon and the Battle of Assaye. He was also responsible for building several forts, including the Fort of Alqueidão, the Fort of Archeira, and the Fort of Arpim. In addition to his military and political achievements, Wellesley founded the Carlton Club and owned the horse Copenhagen. His influence extended into government, where he served as the predecessor to William Lamb, 2nd Viscount Melbourne, during two separate tenures, as well as to Henry Goulburn and John Charles Herries. He was also the prime minister during two tenures of John Copley, 1st Baron Lyndhurst. Furthermore, he was succeeded by F. J. Robinson, 1st Viscount Goderich, John Ponsonby, 4th Earl of Bessborough, and William Lamb, 2nd Viscount Melbourne, in various tenures.

Augustus began his period of activity in 27 BCE. He was the child of Julius Caesar, Gaius Octavius (the father of Augustus), and Atia (the mother of Augustus). Augustus had several children, including Tiberius, Gaius Caesar, and Julia the Elder. Over the course of his life, he was married to Claudia, Livia, and Scribonia. Augustus played a significant role as a military commander, leading forces in the Battle of Actium, the Battle of Forum Gallorum, and the Battle of Mutina. He was succeeded by Tiberius, who regarded Augustus as his predecessor. Additionally, Gnaeus Calpurnius Piso, who served as consul in 23 BCE, also had Augustus as his predecessor. Caesarion, in turn, was succeeded by Augustus.

Barnes Wallis, whose birth name was Barnes Neville Wallis, was born on September 26, 1887, in Ripley, Derbyshire. He became renowned as both an inventor and an engineer, and his career was marked by several significant achievements. Wallis is particularly known for his development of the bouncing bomb, the earthquake bomb, and the geodesic airframe. Over the course of his life, he was recognized with prestigious honors, including the Royal Medal and the Albert Medal from the Royal Society of Arts. Benito Amilcare Andrea Mussolini was born on July 29, 1883, in Predappio. He was the son of Alessandro Mussolini and Rosa Maltoni. Over the course of his life, Mussolini became known as a journalist and was involved in founding several publications, including Il Popolo d'Italia, Il Tevere, and Gerarchia. He also served as the publisher of Il Popolo d'Italia. In addition to his work in journalism, Mussolini was the writer of the film Villafranca and appeared in the film Ways to Strength and Beauty. Mussolini was married to both Ida Dalser and Rachele Mussolini. He was the father of Romano Mussolini, Bruno Mussolini, and Edda Mussolini. Romano Mussolini was his child, and Benito Mussolini was also listed as Romano's parent. Politically, Mussolini was associated with several parties, including the Republican Fascist Party, Fasces of Revolutionary Action, and the Italian Fasces of Combat. He led the Fasci Italiani di Combattimento and was the leader during the tenure of Luigi Gatti and Giovanni Dolfin. He also served as president during the tenures of Francesco Pricolo and Rodolfo Graziani. As prime minister, he was associated with the tenures of Raffaele Guariglia, Renato Ricci, and Dino Grandi. Mussolini was the predecessor to Dino Grandi, Bruno Fornaciari, and Galeazzo Ciano in various tenures, and he was succeeded by Dino Grandi, Luigi Facta, and Paolo Thaon di Revel. Mussolini played a significant role as a commander in several historical events, including the Corfu incident, the Mediterranean and Middle East theatre of World War II, and the Greco-Italian War. He was also associated with the National Republican Army and the National Republican Navy of Italy, both of which were linked to his country. His influence extended to individuals such as Maurice Bardèche, who was influenced by him, and Domenico Leccisi, who became known for his association with Mussolini. Mussolini died in the Kingdom of Italy on April 28, 1945. The cause of his death is recorded as the Death of Benito Mussolini.

Bronisław Malinowski, whose birth name was Bronisław Kasper Malinowski, was born on April 7, 1884, in Austria-Hungary. He held citizenship in both the Austro-Hungarian Empire and Poland, and his nationality was Polish. Malinowski pursued his higher education at the Jagiellonian University and the London School of Economics. Over the course of his career, he became widely known for his contributions to social anthropology, ethnography, and psychological functionalism. Malinowski was influenced by prominent figures such as Charles Gabriel Seligman, James Frazer, and Edvard Westermarck. He also played a significant role as a mentor, serving as the doctoral advisor to Godfrey Wilson, Z. K. Matthews, and Francis L. K. Hsu. Among his own doctoral students were Edmund Leach, Francis L. K. Hsu, and Hilda Kuper. As an author, Malinowski wrote several influential works, including "Argonauts of the Western Pacific," "The Sexual Life of Savages in North-Western Melanesia," and "Coral Gardens and Their Magic." He was married to Valetta Swann. Malinowski died on May 16, 1942, in New Haven, Connecticut.

Caravaggio, whose birth name was Michelangelo Merisi or Amerighi da Caravaggio, was born on September 29, 1571, in the Duchy of Milan. He trained under Simone Peterzano and became renowned in the field of painting. Among his notable works are "Amor Vincit Omnia," "The Seven Works of Mercy," and "The Taking of Christ." A comprehensive list of his paintings is available under the title "List of paintings by Caravaggio." Caravaggio died in Porto Ercole on July 18, 1610. Carl Gustav Jung was born on July 26, 1875, in the Canton of Thurgau. He pursued higher education at the University of Basel and the University of Zurich, where he studied psychology and psychiatry. Jung completed his doctoral studies under the supervision of Eugen Bleuler, who later counted Jung among his doctoral students. Jung himself went on to mentor Sabina Spielrein as her doctoral advisor. Throughout his career, Jung became known for his significant contributions to analytical psychology, the concept of psychological complexes, and the development of Jungian archetypes. His influential works include "Psychological Types," "Memories, Dreams, Reflections," and "Psychology of the Unconscious," all of which he authored. Jung's ideas were shaped by figures such as Carl Gustav Carus, Meister Eckhart, and Friedrich Nietzsche. Jung was recognized for his achievements with awards from the Royal Society of Medicine, the University of Allahabad, and the University of Calcutta. He was married to Emma Jung, and their partnership was reciprocated, as she was also listed as his spouse. Carl Jung died on June 6, 1961, in the Canton of Zürich.

Charlemagne was active from the year 768 until 814. He was the son of Bertrada of Laon and Pepin the Short, succeeding the latter as ruler. Charlemagne was later succeeded by his own son, Louis the Pious. Among his children were Pepin of Italy, Louis the Pious, Charles the Younger, and Rotrude. His spouses included Desiderata of the Lombards, Luitgard, and Fastrada. Charlemagne played a significant role as a commander in several notable conflicts, including the Saxon Wars, the Battle of Roncevaux Pass, and the Siege of Pavia, which took place from 773 to 774. He also founded the Gymnasium Theodorianum. Richbod became known for his association with Charlemagne, and Tekla Teresa Łubieńska produced a notable work about him. Pepin of Italy and Louis the Pious both had Charlemagne as their predecessor, while Carloman I and Desiderius succeeded him.
Charles Babbage was born on December 26, 1791, and died on October 18, 1871, in Marylebone. He studied at Peterhouse, Cambridge, and his academic discipline was political economy. Babbage is particularly known for the Difference Engine, a significant contribution to computing history. He was influenced by several notable figures, including Robert Woodhouse, Gaspard Monge, and John Herschel. Among his children was Benjamin Herschel Babbage. Joseph Clement undertook a significant project related to Babbage, while Allan G. Bromley is recognized for his work concerning Babbage as well.
Charles Robert Darwin was born on February 12, 1809, in Shrewsbury. He became renowned for his contributions to the fields of geology and natural history, and is especially known for works such as "On the Origin of Species," "The Descent of Man, and Selection in Relation to Sex," and "The Voyage of the Beagle." Throughout his career, Darwin was influenced by prominent figures including Alexander von Humboldt, Charles Lyell, and John Herschel. His scholarly achievements were recognized with several prestigious awards, among them the Pour le Mérite, the Royal Medal, and the Copley Medal. Darwin authored several important books, including "Insectivorous Plants," "Geological Observations on South America," and "Geological Observations on the Volcanic Islands." He was married to Emma Darwin, and together they had children, including Horace Darwin and Henrietta Litchfield. His father was Robert Darwin. Charles Darwin died on April 19, 1882, in Downe.
Charles Dickens, whose birth name was Charles John Huffam Dickens, was born on February 7, 1812, in Portsmouth. He became one of the most celebrated English writers, known for notable works such as "David Copperfield," "Nicholas Nickleby," and "Oliver Twist." Dickens was also the author of "American Notes" and "Memoirs of Joseph Grimaldi," and he wrote for adaptations including "Bleak House" (2005 TV serial), "Boy Called Twist," "Little Dorrit" (1924 film), and "David Copperfield" (1913 film). In addition to his literary achievements, he founded The Daily News in the United Kingdom. Dickens was the creator of memorable characters such as Mrs. Bardell from "Pickwick Papers" and Wilkins Micawber, and he contributed to the creation of the "Bleak House" (2005 TV serial). He was married to Catherine Dickens, with whom he had several children, including Dora Annie Dickens, Edward Dickens, and Francis Dickens. Edward Dickens and Walter Landor Dickens were among his children, with Charles Dickens being their parent. Charles Dickens died on June 9, 1870, in Higham, Kent.
Charles Maurice de Talleyrand-Périgord was born in Paris on February 2, 1754, and died in the same city on May 17, 1838. He pursued his education at the Church of Saint-Sulpice in Paris and later attended the University of Paris. Over the course of his career, Talleyrand distinguished himself as a politician, diplomat, and clergyman. He was associated with several political groups, including the Legitimists, the Doctrinaires, and also served as an independent politician. Talleyrand played a significant role in governmental transitions, serving as the predecessor to Charles-Frédéric Reinhard and Pierre Louis Jean Casimir de Blacas during their respective tenures. He was succeeded by Joseph Fouché, Charles-Frédéric Reinhard, and Anne-Adrien-Pierre de Montmorency-Laval in various official capacities.
Charlie Chaplin, whose birth name was Charles Spencer Chaplin Jr., was born in London on April 16, 1889. He was the son of Hannah Chaplin and Charles Chaplin Sr. Over the course of his life, he became known for his extensive career in the entertainment industry, which began in 1899 and continued until 1975. Chaplin passed away in Corsier-sur-Vevey on December 25, 1977. Throughout his life, Chaplin had several spouses, including Mildred Harris, Lita Grey, and Paulette Goddard. He was also the father of Josephine Chaplin, Victoria Chaplin, and Christopher Chaplin. Josephine Chaplin is noted as one of his children, and he is recognized as her parent as well. Chaplin was a multifaceted figure in the world of film and entertainment. He was the creator of The Tramp and was involved in numerous aspects of filmmaking. He directed films such as Modern Times, City Lights, and Monsieur Verdoux, and also served as producer and writer for these works. In addition, he edited films including Modern Times, City Lights, and The Rink. His talents extended to composing music, as he was the music composer for Modern Times, City Lights, and Monsieur Verdoux, and he composed the song "Smile," for which he was also the artist. Chaplin was the composer for "Smile (Charlie Chaplin song)" and contributed as a composer to The Jerry Lewis Show. As an actor, Chaplin starred in films such as Modern Times, City Lights, and Between Showers. He was also the developer of the Montecito Inn and the owner of Manoir de Ban. Furthermore, he was one of the founders of United Artists. Chaplin is known for his association with individuals such as Toraichi Kono and Otis Clark. His legacy is marked by his significant contributions to cinema, both in front of and behind the camera, as well as his influence on the development of the film industry.
Chinua Achebe, whose birth name was Albert Chinụalụmọgụ Achebe, was born on November 16, 1930, in British Nigeria. Christopher Columbus, whose birth name was Cristoforo Colombo, was born in the Republic of Genoa. He became renowned as a maritime explorer and played a significant role in the history of exploration. Columbus was the son of Domenico Colombo and later became the father of Ferdinand Columbus and Diego Columbus. He was married to Filipa Moniz Perestrelo, who was also his spouse. Columbus commanded forces at the Battle of Vega Real and served in positions that were later succeeded by Francisco de Bobadilla and Diego Columbus in different tenures. His life came to an end in Valladolid on May 20, 1506. The legacy of Columbus has been commemorated in notable works, including one by Frank Vittor.

David Lloyd George was born on January 17, 1863, in Chorlton-on-Medlock and died on March 26, 1945, in Llanystumdwy. Asquith succeeded him in several tenures, specifically the first, fourth, and sixth. Enrico Fermi, born on September 29, 1901, was a prominent figure in the field of physics. He pursued his higher education at the Scuola Normale Superiore di Pisa, where he earned a Laurea degree. Over the course of his distinguished career, Fermi became known for significant contributions such as the Thomas–Fermi model, Fermi's golden rule, and the concept of the Fermi problem. His achievements were recognized with several prestigious awards, including the Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, the Medal for Merit, and the Franklin Medal. Fermi served as a doctoral advisor to several notable students, including Sam Treiman, Richard Garwin, and Emilio Segrè. His influence extended beyond his immediate students, impacting figures such as Jorge Allende, Hideki Yukawa, and J. Ernest Wilkins Jr. In his personal life, he was married to Laura Capon Fermi. Fermi's legacy also reached popular culture, as he starred in the film "Atomic Power." He passed away in Chicago on November 28, 1954.

Galileo Galilei, whose birth name was Galileo di Vincenzo Bonaiuti de' Galilei, was born in the Duchy of Florence on February 15, 1564. He became renowned for his contributions to mathematics, engineering, and physics, and was particularly known for his work in observational astronomy, analytical dynamics, and kinematics. Galileo was influenced by figures such as Nicolaus Copernicus and John Philoponus, and in turn, he influenced others, including Robert Boyle. Genghis Khan began his period of activity in 1206. He was the son of Hoelun and Yesügei. Among his children were Ögedei Khan, Tolui, and Alakhai Bekhi. Ögedei Khan was a child of Genghis Khan, and Tolui is recognized as his predecessor.

George Stephenson was born in Northumberland on June 9, 1781, and passed away in Derbyshire on August 12, 1848. George Washington was born in the Colony of Virginia and spent much of his life residing there. He was the son of Augustine Washington and Mary Ball Washington, both of whom counted him among their children. Washington was also the parent of Martha Parke Custis. He married Martha Washington, who was his spouse, and she, in turn, was married to him. Professionally, Washington was engaged in surveying and belonged to the planter class. He was an independent politician and played a significant role in the early history of the United States. His leadership extended to commanding forces in several notable battles, including the Battle of Brandywine, the Battle of Fort Necessity, and the Battle of Fort Washington. He also founded the Culper Ring and was the founder of Pittsburgh. Washington served as a key person for both the Maryland Jockey Club and the First Bank of the United States. Throughout his career, Washington was recognized with several honors, including the Congressional Gold Medal and the Thanks of Congress. He was the employer of Lund Washington, and individuals such as Hercules Posey worked for him. Tobias Lear, William Lee (valet), and Keekyuscung were all known for their association with Washington. The Commander-in-Chief's Guard was connected to his country, and he was the author of George Washington's Farewell Address. Washington's influence extended beyond his lifetime, as Joseph de Maistre was influenced by him. He was also the subject of notable works by Ellen Sharples and Bryant Baker. During his presidency, Joseph Habersham, David Humphreys, and the early life and career of Thomas Jefferson were associated with his tenure. He was the predecessor to John Adams, Henry Knox, and the early life and career of Thomas Jefferson in various tenures, while James Wilkinson succeeded him in another. George Washington died in Virginia on December 14, 1799, with the cause of death being epiglottitis.

Henry II of England reigned from 1154 until 1189. He was the son of Empress Matilda and Geoffrey V, Count of Anjou. During his lifetime, Henry II was married to Eleanor of Aquitaine and was also associated as a spouse with Rosamund Clifford. Among his children were Morgan, who became a bishop, Richard I of England, and Eleanor of England, who became Queen of Castile. Richard I of England was both his son and his successor, while Henry II himself succeeded Stephen, King of England, and was later succeeded by Richard I. William IX, Count of Poitiers, is also noted as both a predecessor and successor in relation to Henry II. He played a commanding role in significant historical events such as the Battle of Crogen, the Revolt of 1173–1174, and The Anarchy. Richard I of England, his son, succeeded him as king, while Stephen, King of England, was his predecessor.

He also played a significant military role, serving as commander during the Rough Wooing, the Battle of the Spurs, and Bigod's Rebellion. Julius Caesar was born on July 12, 100 BCE, and his birth year is recorded as 100 BCE. He was the son of Gaius Julius Caesar, who served as governor of Asia, and Aurelia. Over the course of his life, Caesar held a prominent position, as indicated by his occupation, and was awarded the Civic Crown. He was married to Cornelia, Calpurnia, and Cossutia. Caesar was the father of Caesarion, Augustus, and is also noted as a parent in the early life of Augustus. He played a significant role as a commander in several major conflicts, including Caesar's civil war, the Battle of Alesia, and the Battle of Bibracte. His military and political activities made him a figure of note for individuals such as Cato the Younger, Francesco Carotta, and Rufio, an officer who served under him. Caesar's life came to a violent end through assassination at the Theatre of Pompey on March 15, 44 BCE, with his death year recorded as 44 BCE.

Justus von Liebig was born on May 12, 1803, in the Holy Roman Empire and died on April 20, 1873, in the German Empire, where he also resided during his life. He pursued his academic studies at the University of Bonn and the University of Erlangen, focusing on the discipline of chemistry. Under the guidance of his doctoral advisor, Karl Wilhelm Gottlob Kastner, Liebig developed into a prominent chemist. He later became a mentor himself, supervising doctoral students such as Carl Schmidt, Carl von Voit, and Emil Erlenmeyer. Among those he advised were also Carl Gustav Guckelberger and Carl Remigius Fresenius. Liebig made significant contributions to the field, becoming known for his work on calcium chlorate, advancements in biochemistry, and the invention of the Liebig condenser. His achievements were recognized with the Albert Medal from the Royal Society of Arts. Furthermore, his influence extended to other scientists, including Carl Vogt, Augustus Voelcker, and Henri Victor Regnault, who were notably shaped by his work and ideas.

Leonhard Euler was born in Basel on April 15, 1707, and later died in the Russian Empire on September 18, 1783. Euler himself became an influential academic, guiding Johann Hennert as his doctoral student. His scholarly work spanned the disciplines of mathematics and physics, and he is recognized as the author of "Opera Omnia Leonhard Euler." Euler's impact extended to many prominent figures; Carl Friedrich Gauss, Joseph-Louis Lagrange, and Anders Johan Lexell were all influenced by his work. The academic lineage continued, as Johann Friedrich Hennert, who was advised by Euler, further contributed to the field. Johann Bernoulli, in turn, counted Euler among his own doctoral students, highlighting the significant scholarly connections within this intellectual circle.
Louis Braille was born in Coupvray on January 4, 1809, and is recognized for his significant contribution as the creator of Braille. He pursued his occupation throughout his life until his death in Paris on January 6, 1852. His birth and death years are 1809 and 1852, respectively. The impact of his work is reflected in the fact that J. L. Kaul received an award named after Louis Braille.
Louis-Jacques-Mandé Daguerre, born on November 18, 1787, in Cormeilles-en-Parisis, is best known for his invention of the daguerreotype. He was the author of "The Ruins of Holyrood Chapel." Daguerre died on July 10, 1851, during the period of the French Second Republic. His life spanned from 1787 to 1851.
Louis Pasteur was born in France on December 27, 1822, and also passed away there on September 28, 1895. He was a prominent figure in the fields of biology, mathematics, and physics. Pasteur is renowned for his groundbreaking work on anthrax vaccines, the development of pasteurization, and the formulation of the germ theory of disease. Throughout his distinguished career, he received several notable honors, including the Copley Medal, the Rumford Medal, and the Order of the Medjidie. He was married to Marie Laurent. Pasteur founded both the Pasteur Institute and the Alliance française. His scientific achievements and ideas had a significant influence on figures such as André Chantemesse, Émile Roux, and Alexandre Yersin.
Louis Riel was born on October 22, 1844, in Rupert's Land. He later married Dit name. Riel played a significant leadership role as the commander in several important historical events, including the Red River Rebellion, the North-West Rebellion, and the Battle of Batoche. His influence extended to others, as Honoré Jackson was both employed by Riel and became known for his association with him. Additionally, Andrew Bannatyne's tenure was preceded by Louis Riel. Riel's legacy has been recognized in the arts, with John Cullen Nugent creating a notable work titled "Louis Riel." Riel died on November 16, 1885, in Regina, Saskatchewan.
Louise Arbour was born in Quebec on February 10, 1947. She pursued her education at Collège Regina Assumpta, the Université de Montréal, and the University of Ottawa. Throughout her career, Arbour served in roles where she was succeeded by Peter Cory and Peter Sutherland, while she herself was the predecessor to Louise Charron, Navi Pillay, and Rosalie Abella in their respective tenures.
Lucy Maud Montgomery was born on November 30, 1874, in New London, Prince Edward Island, and held Canadian nationality. She pursued her education at Prince of Wales College and Dalhousie University. Montgomery was active as a writer from 1890 until 1940, contributing significantly to Canadian literature, children's novels, and short fiction. Among her most notable works are "Anne of Green Gables," "Emily of New Moon," and "Rilla of Ingleside." She also authored "Anne's House of Dreams" and "Anne of Avonlea." Montgomery created the character Gilbert Blythe and was the writer for the 1956 film adaptation of "Anne of Green Gables." Additionally, "Bala's Museum" is associated with her name. She passed away in Toronto on April 24, 1942.
Mao Zedong was born on December 26, 1893, in Hunan and later attended Hunan First Normal University. He was affiliated with both the Communist Party of China and the Kuomintang during his political career. Mao had several children, including Li Min, Li Na, and Mao Anlong, all of whom were his offspring. He was married to Luo Yixiu, He Zizhen, and Jiang Qing. Throughout his life, Mao played significant roles in various military engagements, serving as a commander in the Battle of Baitag Bogd, the Battle of Guningtou, and the Battle of the Ch'ongch'on River. He was also the author of influential works such as "On Guerrilla Warfare," "On Contradiction," and "Quotations from Chairman Mao Tse-tung." His leadership extended to being president during one of Jiang Qing's tenures and leader during the tenures of Jiang Qing, Zhang Wentian, and Zhou Enlai. Additionally, he was the predecessor to Zhang Wentian and Zhou Enlai in their fifth tenures, as well as to Liu Shaoqi in his first tenure. Conversely, Li Zongren and Zhang Wentian succeeded him in their respective tenures. Mao's influence reached beyond his immediate political sphere, impacting individuals such as Li Minqi, Lucie Cheng, and Zhang Weiwei, who were influenced by his ideas. He was also known for his association with figures like Stuart R. Schram, Tian Jiaying, and Zhang Zhixin. Mao appeared as a starring figure in works such as "The Autobiography of Nicolae Ceaușescu" and "China: The Roots of Madness." He died in Beijing on September 9, 1976.
Margaret Atwood, whose birth name is Margaret Eleanor Atwood, was born in Ottawa on November 18, 1939. She began her active career in 1961 and has since become a prominent figure in literature, known for her work in genres such as climate fiction, historical fiction, and dystopian fiction. Atwood received her education at the University of Toronto and Radcliffe College. Among her notable works are "Oryx and Crake," "The Testaments," and "Surfacing." Marie Curie, born Maria Salomea Skłodowska on November 7, 1867, in Congress Poland, was a renowned physicist and chemist. She pursued her academic interests under the guidance of her doctoral advisor, Gabriel Lippmann, and later became an influential mentor herself, supervising doctoral students such as Ladislas Goldstein, André-Louis Debierne, and Émile Henriot. Her expertise spanned both physics and chemistry, and her groundbreaking work left a lasting impact on the scientific community. Curie was married to Pierre Curie, and together they had two children, Irène Joliot-Curie and Ève Curie. Her influence extended beyond her immediate family and students; she notably inspired figures such as Moi Meng Ling, William Duane, and Marguerite Perey. Additionally, Branca Edmée Marques and Gioacchino Failla completed their doctoral studies under her supervision. Marie Curie died of aplastic anemia on July 4, 1934, in Passy, Haute-Savoie. Her legacy endures not only through her scientific contributions and the many individuals she influenced but also in institutions bearing her name, such as the Marie Curie charity, which is located at a site associated with her.
Marie Charlotte Carmichael Stopes was born on October 15, 1880, in Edinburgh. She became a prominent figure known for her work in birth control and eugenics, and her academic discipline was palaeobotany. Stopes was the daughter of Charlotte Carmichael Stopes and later became the mother of Harry Stopes-Roe. Marie Stopes authored the influential book "Married Love" and wrote the film "Married Love (film)." Her work had a significant impact, influencing individuals such as Tim Black. Marie Stopes died in Surrey on October 2, 1958.

Nelson Mandela, born as Rolihlahla Mandela on July 18, 1918, in the Union of South Africa, was a prominent figure whose life and achievements left a lasting impact on the world. He pursued his education at the University of Fort Hare, the University of London, and the University of South Africa. Throughout his life, Mandela was associated with the African National Congress and the South African Communist Party. Mandela was married to Evelyn Mase, Winnie Madikizela-Mandela, and Graça Machel. He was the father of Makaziwe Mandela, Makgatho Mandela, and Zindzi Mandela. His leadership extended to various organizations and causes; he was a key person in Mandela and Tambo, and he founded the Peace Parks Foundation, The Elders, and the Nelson Mandela Children's Fund. Nelson Mandela passed away in Johannesburg on December 5, 2013, leaving behind a remarkable legacy of leadership, activism, and dedication to justice.

Niels Henrik David Bohr was born in Copenhagen on October 7, 1885, and he also passed away in the same city. He served as a commander during the Battle of Stalingrad, the Berlin Crisis of 1961, and Project Dark Gene. Owain Glyndŵr was active from 1400 until 1415. He was the son of Gruffydd Fychan II and was married to Margaret Hanmer. Together, they had a daughter named Catrin ferch Owain Glyndŵr. Pablo Picasso was born on October 25, 1881, in Restoration, Spain, and was given the birth name Pablo Diego José Francisco de Paula Juan Nepomuceno María de los Remedios Cipriano de la Santísima Trinidad Ruiz y Picasso. He received his artistic training from José Ruiz y Blasco and the Real Academia de Bellas Artes de San Fernando. Picasso became renowned for his work in several fields, including scenic design, sculpture, and printmaking. Among his most notable works are "The Weeping Woman," "Les Demoiselles d'Avignon," and "Massacre in Korea." He was also the author of pieces such as "Ma Jolie (Picasso, Indianapolis)," "Bottle, Glass, Fork," and "Violon et Raisins." In addition to his contributions to the visual arts, Picasso is credited as the creator of the dish Chicken Picasso. Throughout his life, Picasso had significant personal relationships. He was married to Olga Khokhlova and later to Jacqueline Roque. His children include Claude Picasso, Maya Widmaier-Picasso, and Paloma Picasso. Both Claude and Paloma are his children, and Jacqueline Roque was also his spouse. Picasso's influence extended beyond his own work; Jean Gebser was influenced by him, and the art dealer Paul Rosenberg became known for his association with Picasso. Furthermore, Picasso starred in "The Mystery of Picasso." He passed away in Mougins on April 8, 1973.

Pierre Trudeau, whose birth name was Joseph Philippe Pierre Yves Elliott Trudeau, was born in Quebec on October 18, 1919, and also passed away in Quebec on September 28, 2000. He pursued his education at several distinguished institutions, including Collège Jean-de-Brébeuf, Université de Montréal, and Sciences Po. Professionally, Trudeau was both a jurist and a lawyer. He was affiliated with the Co-operative Commonwealth Federation as well as the Liberal Party of Canada. Trudeau was married to Margaret Trudeau, and together they had three children: Alexandre Trudeau, Justin Trudeau, and Michel Trudeau. Alexandre Trudeau is noted as his son. During his career, Pierre Trudeau served as the commander in the context of "Seven Days to the River Rhine." He also held the position of prime minister during the tenures of Kenneth D. Taylor, Roy MacLaren, and Don Jamieson. In the realm of political succession, Trudeau was the predecessor to Joe Clark in both the first and second tenures of Clark, as well as to John Turner in Turner’s first tenure. Conversely, he succeeded Lester B. Pearson in both the first and second tenures of Pearson, and was also the successor to Joe Clark in Clark’s first tenure.
Pierre de Coubertin, whose birth name was Pierre de Frédy, was born in Paris on January 1, 1863. He was a French national and attended Sciences Po as his alma mater. De Coubertin is renowned for founding the International Olympic Committee. He served as president, with David R. Francis succeeding him in this role, and was also the predecessor to Henri de Baillet-Latour and Sigfrid Edström during their respective tenures. Plato was born in Ancient Greece in 428 BCE and died there in 348 BCE. He is associated with the tradition of Western philosophy and was influenced by figures and movements such as Pythagoras, the Eleusinian Mysteries, and Archytas. Benedict XVI resided in Vatican City while serving as pope. He succeeded John Paul II and was later succeeded by Pope Francis. Notably, Angelo Sodano's predecessor was Pope Benedict XVI. Pope Gregory XIII, born Ugo Boncompagni on January 7, 1502, in Bologna, was educated at the University of Bologna. He later became the father of Giacomo Boncompagni. Gregory XIII succeeded Pope Pius V and was, in turn, succeeded by Pope Sixtus V, who regarded Gregory XIII as his predecessor. Pope Gregory XIII died in Rome on April 10, 1585. His papal motto was "Aperuit et clausit," which translates as "Opened and closed."
Pope Leo IX, born as Bruno von Egisheim-Dagsburg on June 21, 1002, in the Holy Roman Empire, served as the head of the Catholic Church following Pope Damasus II. He died in Rome on April 19, 1054. After his death, he was succeeded by Pope Victor II, for whom Leo IX was also the predecessor. Pope Leo IX is recognized as a saint in Guardia Lombardi.

Qin Shi Huang began his active years in 221 BCE and was the son of Queen Dowager Zhao and King Zhuangxiang of Qin. He had two children, Fusu and Qin Er Shi. Clinton Richard Dawkins was born on March 26, 1941, in Nairobi. He studied at the University of Oxford, where he earned a Master of Arts and a Doctor of Philosophy. His doctoral advisor was Nikolaas Tinbergen, who also influenced his work, along with Christopher Hitchens and W. D. Hamilton. Dawkins himself later became the doctoral advisor to Alan Grafen and Mark Ridley, and he was a doctoral student of Nikolaas Tinbergen. Dawkins is widely recognized for his contributions to the understanding of memes, the gene-centered view of evolution, and his criticism of religion. He is the author of several notable works, including "An Appetite for Wonder," "The Ancestor's Tale," and "The Root of All Evil?," the latter of which he also starred in. Throughout his career, Dawkins has received numerous honors, such as the International Cosmos Prize, recognition from the Zoological Society of London, and the title of Fellow of the Royal Society. He founded the Richard Dawkins Foundation for Reason and Science, where he is also a key figure. In his personal life, Dawkins has been married to Lalla Ward and Marian Dawkins.

Sigmund Freud, born as Sigismund Schlomo Freud on May 6, 1856, in the Austrian Empire, was a prominent figure in the fields of psychoanalysis, neurology, and psychotherapy. He attended the University of Vienna, which served as his alma mater. Freud became widely known for his foundational work in psychoanalysis, as well as for his theories on repression in psychology and the Oedipus complex. His intellectual development was influenced by thinkers such as Schopenhauer, Josef Breuer, and Empedocles. Freud was married to Martha Bernays, and together they had children, including Ernst L. Freud and Anna Freud. Anna Freud, in turn, was his daughter. Throughout his distinguished career, Freud received several honors, including the Royal Society award and the Goethe Prize. He was the author of significant works such as "On Narcissism," "Beyond the Pleasure Principle," and "Introduction to Psychoanalysis." Freud passed away in Hampstead on September 23, 1939.
Skanderbeg, whose period of activity began and ended in 1443, was a prominent figure associated with both the League of Lezhë and the Principality of Kastrioti. He was the son of Voisava Kastrioti and Gjon Kastrioti, succeeding his father and later being succeeded by his own child, Gjon Kastrioti II. Skanderbeg was married to Donika Kastrioti, with whom he had Gjon Kastrioti II. He played a significant role as the commander in several battles, including the Battle of Albulena, the Battle of Mokra in 1445, and the Battle of Mokra in July 1462. Additionally, Skanderbeg was responsible for building the Castle of Rodon. Voisava Kastrioti is notably recognized for her connection to Skanderbeg, while Donika Kastrioti was his spouse.
Slavoj Žižek was born on March 21, 1949, in Ljubljana. He is associated with Western philosophy and has been influenced by figures such as Carl Schmitt and Baruch Spinoza, as well as by the Book of Job. Žižek is the author of several works, including "The Fright of Real Tears," "The Sublime Object of Ideology," and "Pandemic!" He is married to Jela Krečič.
