Socrates was born in the deme, a subdivision of ancient Athens, in the year 470 BCE. He died in Classical Athens in 399 BCE. As a prominent figure in Western philosophy, Socrates was influenced by several thinkers, including Prodicus, Damon of Athens, and Anaxagoras.
Stan Rogers was a solo singer born in Hamilton, Ontario, who was active in the music industry from 1970 until 1983. He was closely associated with the folk music genre and worked with record labels such as Borealis Records, Fogarty's Cove Music, and RCA Records. Rogers founded Fogarty's Cove Music himself. Throughout his career, he was connected with Garnet Rogers and Nathan Rogers, both as associated bands and as associated musical artists. In turn, Nathan Rogers was also associated with Stan Rogers as both a band and a musical artist. Stan Rogers was the artist and writer behind notable songs including "Barrett's Privateers," "The Mary Ellen Carter," and "Make and Break Harbour." In addition to his musical achievements, he authored the book "Northwest Passage." Rogers passed away in Hebron, Kentucky.
Stephen Hawking was born on January 8, 1942, in Oxford and passed away in Cambridge on March 14, 2018. He was married to Jane Hawking, and together they had a child named Lucy Hawking. Hawking’s academic pursuits were centered on general relativity and quantum gravity. He completed his doctoral studies under the supervision of Dennis W. Sciama and later became a doctoral advisor himself to students such as Christophe Galfard, Gary Gibbons, Bernard Carr, and Malcolm John Perry. Gary Gibbons and Malcolm John Perry both had Hawking as their doctoral advisor, while Christophe Galfard was not only his student but was also influenced by him, as were Sasha Haco and Werner Israel. Hawking was widely recognized for his contributions, with Neil Turok being known for his association with him. In addition to his scientific work, Hawking was involved in various creative projects. He was the author of several books, including "The Physics of Star Trek," "The Universe in a Nutshell," and "My Brief History." He also contributed as a writer to the 2013 film "Hawking." His presence extended to the screen, starring in productions such as "Brave New World with Stephen Hawking," "God, the Universe and Everything Else," and "A Brief History of Time" (film). Furthermore, he was featured as an artist in the "Symphony of Science."
Steven Arthur Pinker was born on September 18, 1954, in Quebec. He pursued his education at McGill University and later at Harvard University. Over the course of his life, Pinker has been married to Nancy Etcoff, a psychologist, as well as to Rebecca Goldstein. As an accomplished author, he has written several notable works, including "Enlightenment Now," "How the Mind Works," and "The Better Angels of Our Nature."
Steven Weinberg, born on May 3, 1932, was a prominent figure in theoretical physics. He was known for his significant contributions to the field, particularly for his work on the Joos–Weinberg equation, the electroweak interaction, and the concept of the axion. Throughout his distinguished career, Weinberg received several prestigious awards, including the Breakthrough Prize, the Andrew Gemant Award, and the Elliott Cresson Medal. Weinberg completed his doctoral studies under the supervision of Sam Treiman, and he later became a mentor himself, serving as the doctoral advisor to John Preskill and Edward Tryon. His academic influence extended further, as he was also a doctoral student of Sam Treiman. In addition to his scientific achievements, Weinberg was an accomplished author, writing works such as "Cosmology," "Lake Views: This World and the Universe," and "The First Three Minutes." He also appeared in the film "Nobelity." On a personal note, Steven Weinberg was married to Louise Weinberg, who was also his spouse. He passed away in Austin, Texas, on July 23, 2021.
Stompin' Tom Connors, also known by the alias Tommy Messer, was born on February 9, 1936, in Saint John, New Brunswick. He later became associated with Skinners Pond, Prince Edward Island, which is recognized as his hometown. Connors was a solo singer whose musical career spanned from 1988 until 2013, during which he was active in the genres of folk music, country music, and Canadiana. He was closely linked to Boot Records, both as an instrument and as a record label, and he also released music under the EMI label. Notably, Connors founded Boot Records himself. Throughout his career, Stompin' Tom Connors was the artist behind songs such as "Moon-Man Newfie," "Ketchup Song (Stompin' Tom Connors song)," and "The Hockey Song." He not only performed these songs but also wrote them, and in the case of "The Hockey Song," he served as the composer as well. Additionally, he was the music composer and star of "This Is Stompin' Tom." Stompin' Tom Connors passed away on March 6, 2013, in Ballinafad, Ontario.

Thomas Alva Edison was born on February 11, 1847, in Milan, Ohio. He later became known for his significant contributions to technology and innovation, particularly for inventions such as the electric pen, electric power distribution systems, and the nickel–iron battery. Edison attended Cooper Union during his education and began his active professional years in 1877, continuing until 1930. Over the course of his life, he founded several notable companies, including Continental Edison, Thomas A. Edison, Inc., and the Edison Illuminating Company. Edison was also involved in the early film industry, serving as the director of "President McKinley Inauguration Footage" and producing films such as "Monsieur" (1911), "Frankenstein" (1910), and "The Monroe Doctrine" (1896). His influence extended beyond his own work, as he was the doctoral advisor to Carl Chang, a computer scientist, and influenced individuals like Changjoon Justin Lee. Additionally, he was recognized as a key person at SAE International. In his personal life, Edison was the father of Theodore Miller Edison, Charles Edison, and Madeleine Edison. Charles Edison, in turn, was his child. Edison's birth name was Thomas Alva Edison, and he lived until October 18, 1931, passing away in West Orange, New Jersey. His life spanned from 1847 to 1931. For reference, his IMDb identification number is 0249379, and his occupation is recorded as Thomas Edison Person Function 1.
Thomas Loren Friedman was born in the United States on July 20, 1953. Thomas More was born on February 7, 1478, in the City of London. He was the son of John More, a judge, and later became the father of Margaret Roper. More received his education at the University of Oxford. He married Alice More, who was also his spouse, and together they formed a notable family. Throughout his life, Thomas More made significant contributions as an author, writing works such as "Utopia," "A Dialogue of Comfort against Tribulation," and "Defence of the Seven Sacraments." His influence extended beyond his writings, as figures like Joseph de Maistre, Leo Strauss, and Simone Weil were influenced by his ideas. Pieter Gillis is known for his association with Thomas More. More held important positions during his career, serving as chancellor under the tenure of John Russell, 1st Earl of Bedford. He was also the predecessor to Thomas Audley, 1st Baron Audley of Walden, in three separate tenures. In addition to his political and literary achievements, Thomas More founded St Thomas More Language College, and he is recognized as the patron saint of Thomas More College in South Australia. Thomas More died on July 6, 1535, at Tower Hill. His legacy endures through his family, his works, and the institutions and individuals he influenced.
Tim Berners-Lee, whose birth name is Timothy John Berners-Lee, was born in London on June 8, 1955. He is also known by the aliases TBL and TimBL. His parents are Conway Berners-Lee and Mary Lee Woods, both of whom have Tim as their child. He received his education at The Queen's College, Oxford. Throughout his distinguished career, Tim Berners-Lee has been recognized with several prestigious awards, including the Order of Merit, the Turing Award, and the ACM Software System Award. He is the author of Libwww, the Line Mode Browser, and CERN httpd, and he developed the WorldWideWeb. In addition to his technical contributions, he founded the Open Data Institute and the World Wide Web Foundation, where he is also a key person. Tim Berners-Lee is a key figure at Proton AG as well. His influence extends to individuals such as James Hendler, who has been influenced by his work. Tim Berners-Lee is married to Rosemary Leith.

Umar was the child of Al-Khattab ibn Nufayl and Hantamah bint Hisham. He was the father of Ubayd Allah ibn Umar, Zayd ibn Umar, and Abd Allah ibn Umar ibn al-Khattab. Umar’s period of activity both began and ended in the year 23. He succeeded Abu Bakr and was, in turn, succeeded by Uthman, while Uthman’s predecessor was also Umar. Abu Bakr’s successor was Umar as well. Umar was known as the employer of Miqdad ibn Aswad and Al-Bara' ibn Malik. Vasco da Gama was born in Alentejo and died in Cochin on December 24, 1524. He was the son of Estêvão da Gama, who is notably recognized for his connection to Vasco da Gama. Vasco da Gama himself was the father of Cristóvão da Gama and Estêvão da Gama, who lived during the 16th century. He held a prominent position among the colonial heads of Portuguese India and served as a commander during the Battle of Calicut in 1503. Following the tenure of Duarte de Menezes, Vasco da Gama succeeded him in office. The name Vasco da Gama is also associated with various sports teams and organizations. Vladimir Lenin, born as Vladimir Ilyich Ulyanov in Ulyanovsk, was a Russian national who played a pivotal role in the history of the Soviet Union. He was the son of Maria Alexandrovna Ulyanova and Ilya Ulyanov, both of whom are known for their association with him. Lenin studied at Saint Petersburg State University before embarking on a political career that would see him become a central figure in several revolutionary movements. He was married to Nadezhda Krupskaya, who is also recognized as his spouse. Lenin was a member of the Bolsheviks, the Communist Party of the Soviet Union, and the Russian Social Democratic Labour Party. He founded the newspaper Iskra and authored significant works such as "The Development of Capitalism in Russia," "Left-Wing" Communism: An Infantile Disorder, and "What Is to Be Done?" His leadership extended to commanding roles during the July Days, the 1905 Russian Revolution, and the Russian Civil War. Lenin served as the leader of the Council of People's Commissars of the Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic and later of the Council of People's Commissars of the Soviet Union. He was the predecessor to Alexei Rykov in two separate tenures and held the position of prime minister during the tenures of Pyotr Bogdanov, Pyotr Kobozev, and Pēteris Stučka. His influence reached far beyond his lifetime, shaping the thoughts of figures such as José Carlos Mariátegui, Paul Sweezy, and Richard D. Wolff. Lenin died on January 21, 1924, in Gorki Leninskiye.
Voltaire, whose birth name was François-Marie Arouet, was born in Paris on November 21, 1694. He also died in Paris, passing away on May 30, 1778. He attended the Collège Louis-le-Grand as his alma mater. Voltaire was the author of several notable works, including "Candide," "L'Ingénu," and "Letters on the English." In addition to his literary achievements, he founded the Manufacture royale. His influence extended to figures such as Denis Diderot, Joseph de Maistre, and Jules Michelet. Voltaire is also recognized as the genre associated with Tekla Teresa Łubieńska. Furthermore, André-Joseph Panckoucke and Marie Louise Mignot are known for their connection to Voltaire.
Václav Havel was born on October 5, 1936, in Prague. He pursued his education at the Faculty of Theatre in Prague as well as the Czech Technical University in Prague. Over the course of his life, Havel was married to Olga Havlová and later to Dagmar Havlová, who was also his spouse. He was associated with the Civic Forum political party. Havel was a prominent figure in Czech political and cultural life. He served as president during the tenures of Josef Tošovský, Luboš Dobrovský, and Jaroslav Bašta. He succeeded Gustáv Husák and was, in turn, the predecessor to Václav Klaus. In addition to his political career, Havel was an accomplished writer and playwright. He authored works such as "The Memorandum" and "Temptation," and in 2011, he both wrote and directed the film "Leaving." Václav Havel passed away on December 18, 2011, in Vlčice, located in the Trutnov District.

Werner Karl Heisenberg was born on December 5, 1901, in the German Empire. He pursued his studies at the University of Göttingen and the University of Munich, where he was mentored by Arnold Sommerfeld as his doctoral advisor. Heisenberg became a prominent figure in theoretical physics and is especially known for his contributions to the canonical commutation relation, quantum field theory, and quantum fluctuation. Over the course of his career, he received several prestigious awards, including the Barnard Medal for Meritorious Service to Science, the Matteucci Medal, and the Pour le Mérite for Sciences and Arts. Heisenberg also played a significant role as an academic mentor. Among his doctoral students were Reinhard Oehme, Edward Teller, and Friedwardt Winterberg. He further influenced the scientific community by serving as the doctoral advisor to Rudolf Peierls and Rudolf Schulten. His impact extended beyond his direct students, as both Jane Dewey and Manfred Eigen were influenced by his work. In addition to his research and teaching, Heisenberg authored "The Physical Principles of the Quantum Theory." He was the father of Jochen Heisenberg and Martin Heisenberg. Werner Heisenberg died in Bavaria on February 1, 1976.
Wilfrid Laurier, whose birth name was Henri Charles Wilfrid Laurier, was born on November 20, 1841, in Canada East. He pursued his education at McGill University and was affiliated with both the Liberal Party of Canada and the Laurier Liberals. Laurier was married to Zoé Laurier, and this relationship was mutual, as Zoé Laurier was also his spouse. He passed away in Ottawa on February 17, 1919. Throughout his career, Laurier played a significant role in Canadian politics. He served as the predecessor to Désiré Olivier Bourbeau, William John Watts, and Ernest Lapointe during their respective tenures. Additionally, he was the prime minister during the tenures of Leverett George DeVeber, Donald Smith, 1st Baron Strathcona and Mount Royal, and John Hamilton-Gordon, 1st Marquess of Aberdeen and Temair. After his service, Laurier was succeeded by Joseph-Arthur Lortie, Edward Blake, and Edward John Hemming in their respective tenures. Laurier’s legacy also extends to education, as Wilfrid Laurier is noted as the college attended by Scott Hutter, a Canadian football player.

Kolff received several prestigious honors, such as the Gairdner Foundation International Award, the Wilhelm Exner Medal, and the Harvey Prize. He passed away in Pennsylvania on February 11, 2009.

William Harvey was born on April 1, 1578, in Folkestone and died on June 3, 1657, in Roehampton. He was a prominent figure in the fields of anatomy and medicine, and is especially known for his work on systemic circulation as well as for his influential publication, "Exercitatio Anatomica de Motu Cordis et Sanguinis in Animalibus." Harvey studied under Hieronymus Fabricius, who served as his doctoral advisor, and in turn, Harvey was Fabricius's doctoral student. His legacy extended beyond his own research; he founded The Harvey Grammar School and played a key role in the Harvey Society. William Harvey's work had a significant impact on later thinkers, influencing figures such as René Descartes and Pierre Louis Maupertuis. Additionally, Colin MacDougall succeeded him in a particular tenure, with Harvey serving as his predecessor.
William Lyon Mackenzie King was born on December 17, 1874, in Berlin, Ontario, and died on July 22, 1950, in Chelsea, Quebec. He was affiliated with the Liberal Party of Canada and pursued his education at University College, Toronto, as well as the University of Chicago, where he earned a Master of Arts degree. King played a significant role in the Federal Woodlands Preservation League, serving as a key person within the organization. Bennett in two separate tenures and to Edward LeRoy Bowerman in one tenure. Conversely, he succeeded John Alexander Macdonald Armstrong, as well as R. B. Bennett in two different tenures. Winston Churchill was born on November 30, 1874, in Blenheim, Oxfordshire, and was given the birth name Winston Leonard Spencer Churchill. He was the son of Lord Randolph Churchill and Jennie Jerome. Churchill received his education at Harrow School and later at the Royal Military College, Sandhurst. He married Clementine Churchill, with whom he had several children, including Sarah Churchill, who became an actress, Mary Soames, and Diana Churchill. Mary Soames was also his daughter. Throughout his life, Churchill was associated with both the Conservative Party (UK) and the Liberal Party (UK). He was recognized with numerous honors, collectively known as the Honours of Winston Churchill. His professional pursuits were diverse, as he was known both as a painter and as a writer. Among his literary works are "The Story of the Malakand Field Force," "The River War," and "Tower of the Koutoubia Mosque," all of which he authored. He also served as the editor of the British Gazette and was the writer of the 1964 film "The Finest Hours." Churchill played significant roles in various historical events, serving as commander during the Belfast Blitz, the Dekemvriana, and the Mau Mau rebellion. His influence extended to others, as Grace Hamblin, Theresa Garnett, and James Klugmann were all known for their association with him. Additionally, Louise Zarmati received an award named after Winston Churchill. Several artists, including David Jagger, Stella Marks, and Alfred Egerton Cooper, created notable works featuring Churchill. In the realm of government and public service, he was the predecessor to Reginald McKenna, E. D. Morel, and Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis, in various tenures. He also served as prime minister during the tenures of Lionel Heald, Quintin Hogg, Baron Hailsham of St Marylebone, and Reginald Manningham-Buller, 1st Viscount Dilhorne. Churchill was succeeded in different roles by Reginald McKenna, David Grenfell, and David Lloyd George. Winston Churchill passed away on January 24, 1965.
Wole Soyinka, whose birth name is Akínwándé Olúwolé Babátúndé Sóyíinká, was born on July 13, 1934, in Abeokuta. He began his active career in 1957 and received his education at Abeokuta Grammar School and the University of Leeds. Soyinka is the author of several notable works, including "Death and the King's Horseman," "The Interpreters," and "Season of Anomy." In addition to his literary achievements, he starred in the film "Kongi's Harvest" and the documentary "Fuelling Poverty," and also served as the writer for "Kongi's Harvest." Grace Eniola Soyinka is his child.
Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart is recognized as the author of the musical "The Magic Flute." He is also credited as the composer for several works, including "Payback 2," "Mozart on Tour," and the television series "Whiz Kids." In addition, Mozart composed the music for "Quiet Night In," the 2003 film "Eroica," and the 1975 film adaptation of "The Magic Flute." His influence extended to figures such as Dietrich von Hildebrand, who was influenced by him. Cäcilia Weber is known for her association with Mozart. Regarding his family, Anna Maria Mozart was his mother, while Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart and Karl Thomas Mozart were his children. Mozart also contributed as a writer to songs such as "Leck mich im Arsch" by Insane Clown Posse and "Lacrymosa."
